Of all the metallic alloys in use today, the alloys of iron (\n       <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">\n        steel\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">\n        stainless steel\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cast_iron" title="Cast iron">\n        cast iron\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tool_steel" title="Tool steel">\n        tool steel\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Alloy_steel" title="Alloy steel">\n        alloy steels\n       </a>\n       ) make up the largest proportion both by quantity and commercial value. Iron alloyed with various proportions of carbon gives low, mid and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_carbon_steel" title="High carbon steel">\n        high carbon steels\n       </a>\n       . An iron-carbon alloy is only considered steel if the carbon level is between 0.01% and 2.00%. For the steels, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hardness" title="Hardness">\n        hardness\n       </a>\n       and tensile strength of the steel is related to the amount of carbon present, with increasing carbon levels also leading to lower ductility and toughness. Heat treatment processes such as quenching and tempering can significantly change these properties, however. Cast Iron is defined as an iron\xe2\x80\x93carbon alloy with more than 2.00% but less than 6.67% carbon. Stainless steel is defined as a regular steel alloy with greater than 10% by weight alloying content of Chromium. Nickel and Molybdenum are typically also found in stainless steels.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other significant metallic alloys are those of\n       <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">\n        aluminium\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Titanium" title="Titanium">\n        titanium\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">\n        copper\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Magnesium" title="Magnesium">\n        magnesium\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copper_alloys" title="Copper alloys">\n        Copper alloys\n       </a>\n       have been known for a long time (since the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">\n        Bronze Age\n       </a>\n       ), while the alloys of the other three metals have been relatively recently developed. Due to the chemical reactivity of these metals, the electrolytic extraction processes required were only developed relatively recently. The alloys of aluminium, titanium and magnesium are also known and valued for their high strength-to-weight ratios and, in the case of magnesium, their ability to provide electromagnetic shielding. These materials are ideal for situations where high strength-to-weight ratios are more important than bulk cost, such as in the aerospace industry and certain automotive engineering applications.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Semiconductors">\n        Semiconductors\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Materials_science&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Semiconductors">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The study of semiconductors is a significant part of materials science. A\n       <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor" title="Semiconductor">\n        semiconductor\n       </a>\n       is a material that has a resistivity between a metal and insulator. Its electronic properties can be greatly altered through intentionally introducing impurities or doping. From these semiconductor materials, things such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Diode" title="Diode">\n        diodes\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">\n        transistors\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">\n        light-emitting diodes\n       </a>\n       (LEDs), and analog and digital\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_circuit" title="Electric circuit">\n        electric circuits\n       </a>\n       can be built, making them materials of interest in industry. Semiconductor devices have replaced thermionic devices (vacuum tubes) in most applications. Semiconductor devices are manufactured both as single discrete devices and as\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">\n        integrated circuits\n       </a>\n       (ICs), which consist of a number\xe2\x80\x94from a few to millions\xe2\x80\x94of devices manufactured and interconnected on a single semiconductor substrate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Of all the semiconductors in use today,\n       <a href="/wiki/Silicon" title="Silicon">\n        silicon\n       </a>\n       makes up the largest portion both by quantity and commercial value. Monocrystalline silicon is used to produce wafers used in the semiconductor and electronics industry. Second to silicon,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gallium_arsenide" title="Gallium arsenide">\n        gallium arsenide\n       </a>\n       (GaAs) is the second most popular semiconductor used. Due to its higher electron mobility and saturation velocity compared to silicon, it is a material of choice for high-speed electronics applications. These superior properties are compelling reasons to use GaAs circuitry in mobile phones, satellite communications, microwave point-to-point links and higher frequency radar systems. Other semiconductor materials include\n       <a href="/wiki/Germanium" title="Germanium">\n        germanium\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Silicon_carbide" title="Silicon carbide">\n        silicon carbide\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gallium_nitride" title="Gallium nitride">\n        gallium nitride\n       </a>\n       and have various applications.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Relation_to_other_fields">\n        Relation to other fields\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Materials_science&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Relation to other fields">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Materials science evolved\xe2\x80\x94starting from the 1960s\xe2\x80\x94because it was recognized that to create, discover and design new materials, one had to approach it in a unified manner. Thus, materials science and engineering emerged at the intersection of various fields such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">\n        metallurgy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solid_state_physics" title="Solid state physics">\n        solid state physics\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">\n        chemistry\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">\n        chemical engineering\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">\n        mechanical engineering\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">\n        electrical engineering\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The field is inherently\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interdisciplinary" title="Interdisciplinary">\n        interdisciplinary\n       </a>\n       , and the materials scientists/engineers must be aware and make use of the methods of the physicist, chemist and engineer. The field thus maintains close relationships with these fields. Also, many physicists, chemists and engineers also find themselves working in materials science.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The overlap between physics and materials science has led to the offshoot field of\n       <i>\n        materials physics\n       </i>\n       , which is concerned with the physical properties of materials. The approach is generally more macroscopic and applied than in\n       <a href="/wiki/Condensed_matter_physics" title="Condensed matter physics">\n        condensed matter physics\n       </a>\n       . See\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_publications_in_physics#Materials_physics" title="List of publications in physics">\n        important publications in materials physics\n       </a>\n       for more details on this field of study.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The field of materials science and engineering is important both from a scientific perspective, as well as from an engineering one. When discovering new materials, one encounters new phenomena that may not have been observed before. Hence, there is a lot of science to be discovered when working with materials. Materials science also provides a test for theories in condensed matter physics.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Materials are of the utmost importance for engineers, as the usage of the appropriate materials is crucial when designing systems. As a result, materials science is an increasingly important part of an engineer\'s education.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Emerging_technologies_in_materials_science">\n        Emerging technologies in materials science\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Materials_science&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Emerging technologies in materials science">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Emerging technology\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Status\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Potentially marginalized technologies\n        </th>\n insulation, insulative glass if it can be made clear, sleeves for oil pipelines, aerospace, high-heat &amp; extreme cold applications\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n   <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Kevlar" title="Kevlar">\n          Kevlar\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Armor\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n prototypes\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Conductors\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Lighter and cheaper wires, antistatic materials,\n         <a href="/wiki/Organic_solar_cell" </td>\n        <td>\n         Hypothetical\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Present nuclear\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         New materials; nuclear weapons, power\n        </td>\n
